Oh, children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, because it has reached its end through me and my consequences, and through my explanations and declarations, it seems to me that you should complete that which is in this treatise, which is part of my surgery.
Since my surgery is neglected in our region and in our time, completely private, so that the science of it is almost forgotten, and its practice remains hidden; and there remain only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which are changed to the most part and added to those errors and aberrations, until the intentions of it are closed and its force and art are elongated.
And it seems to me that you should revive that ancient order of this treatise in accordance with the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that you may acquire the forms of the instruments of cauterization and other tools of the craft as if by addition to the declaration, and for preparation thereto, which is necessary.
However, the reason why there is not found a good craftsman in our time who has mastery of his hand in this art, is that the art of medicine is long and tedious, and it requires one's actor to be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen recognized, so that he may know the joints of the members and their forms, and the conjunction and separation of them; and have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, and their number, and the arrangement of them; and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their efflux.
And therefore Hippocrates says that a name is not a motive, but rather in small work, and most of all in the art of surgery.
But we have already spoken of that in the introduction to this book; for one who is not skilled in what we have said about anatomy is not fit to be a surgeon, lest he fall into error by which men will die, as I have seen many of those who are thus formed in this science and gain nothing from it, but rather lose their science and experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who had inserted an abscess of scrophulous humor into the neck of a woman, and he had cut through some arteries of the neck so that a great deal of blood flowed, whereby the woman died between them.
And I saw another doctor who thought he would pull out an abscess from a man's groin which had developed in his state, and the abscess was large, and it came to him and removed that abscess with a piece of the bladder, whereby that man died on the third day.
And I had already called out to him to remove it, and I saw that because of the size of the abscess and the condition of the patient he knew it would kill him.
And I saw another doctor who took a stipend from a duke in our land for surgery, and he proceeded to operate on a blacksmith's son who had a fracture in his thigh; and the doctor, with his ignorance, extracted the bone, placing it above the wound, using pillows and splints with excessive tension, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then he released the dressing according to his own desires, and released the splint, and released it for several days, commanding that we remove the bandage; and it happened thus that the thigh and leg became inflamed, and perished.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to remove the bandage, and achieving calmness and easing his pains.
But meanwhile corruption was confirmed in the member, so that I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to corrupt the member until the patient perished.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous abscess, and made it ulcerate after some days, until the pus magnified the evil of it with its lord.
Which cause is that the cancerous part is pure of melancholic humor, whereas it does not need to be brought to him with all force, but rather should be left as a member which suffers and is completely hostile.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you that the surgery with me be divided into two divisions: one is in operation which is associated with health, and the other is in work where danger is involved in the greatest circumstances.
And I have already existed here in every place of this book where operation is in the wrong and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to keep this and set aside that, so that foolish ones do not find a way to speak and to deceive you.
And therefore take up your own arms with solicitude and protection of God, and your own patients with felicity and firmness.
And use the best method by the grace of God to achieve health and praiseworthy success, and put aside terrible diseases that are difficult to heal, and keep your own arms away from this which makes you fear, so that you may situate yourself in your faith and in your own name, not being deceived: for it remains to your glory, and even more so in the world and finally to your sanctity.
Galen already said in some of his own writings: "Do not heal bad diseases, lest you be called a bad doctor."
And I have divided this book into three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and the first part of the first chapter. The first chapter, ordered by the head to the feet, in the forms of instruments and in the furnishings of cauterization, and from which it is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on dryness and puncturing, and on sponges, and wounds, and extraction of splinters and similar things, all chaptered and ordered according to the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on curing of fractures and similar things; chapter ordered from head to feet, and according to the forms of instruments.
I should say what quality the joints have of that cauterization and what injuries it inflicts on them, and in what condition cauterization is prohibited.
So I say that the discourse on the quality of the joints in cauterization and its injuries is a long and prolix sermon, subtle by science, and secret and hidden; and already many wise men have spoken about it, and some have disagreed with each other, and for my part, I will only briefly touch on some of their sermons, fearing prolongation.
And so I say that cauterization is suitable for all complete configurations universally, which are in material or its materials, except for two configurations, which are configurations of dry matter.
In the dry and withered configuration of material, it will desiccate; for some would say that cauterization is beneficial to it, while others would say the opposite of it, that cauterization is not suitable in a disease which is caused by quality and dryness, for nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that a dry and withered configuration with water that is hot and dry should be healed.
And say that the one who says the opposite of it is wrong, that by cauterization it is made healthy in all dry and withered diseases that are found in the bodies of men, for when you compare the human body and its humidity to the configuration of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I say by this sermon that this experiment is already known to me on several occasions to uncover.
But meanwhile it is not necessary that this come to be written again in detail, since it has already been exposed and exercised in the chapter on cauterization for the last exercise, and understood the diversity of human configurations and the disposition of diseases in their own bodies, and the causes of these, and their accidents, and the space of time for these.
But in other configurations, there is no fear on your part, and especially in cold and humid diseases, for all doctors have already agreed on these, and are not in discord about the joint treatment with cauterization in those.
And know, children, that the secret of healing through cauterization with fire and its goodness is that on top of cauterization with medicine, it is combined because fire is simple, the action of which only reaches the member that is being cauterized and does not harm another member that is adjusted to it except for a little damage.
But the action of medicine combined reaches that member which is distant from it, and very quickly brings disease of difficult healing to the sick member, and very quickly increases suffering.
But the fire, by its sublimity and goodness of substance, does not do this except to superfluously. And it is already known to us through experience and the length of service in studying the art about the truth of causes; and therefore I am excused from the length of this sermon. But if it were not for the fact that it is not read well in this pause, I would reveal to you a secret hidden in the fire, and the quality of its operation in the body, and its expulsion by which it expels diseases, with a philosophical demonstrative sermon, which would be sharp in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time when it is suitable to perform cauterization and pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at any time, because the harm caused by the accident of time is submerged in the joint of what is attracted to cauterization, and even more so if the cauterization is for necessary pains or necessary torments, which do not suffer delay because they are feared of those who come with evil, which is greater than small damage entering through time.
And thus it does not sit in your minds, or, children, this is not esteemed except by the common people and foolish doctors, so that to that disease which is cured by cauterization there is no reduction of time, and pause is taken for the consequence.
And the cause is not thus, as they think by this, because cauterization is only in a place of medicine that alters the configuration and dries out the humors which are the cause why pains come.
But meanwhile, cauterization is excessive above medicine by virtue of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that his disease may return at some hour of time, according to the configuration of the patient and the location of his disease, and the virtue of him, and what is prepared in his body through the accumulation of superfluidities there, and what is brought to him through acquisition of victuals and similar things to those causes; but if the disease that is administered cauterization is a subtle disease in a member with few superfluidities and humors, just as cauterization of teeth for pain and similar things, it is possible that in him that pain may not return, but rather it will be reduced.
And besides, it is common speech that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, and it is a dubious saying, not in what I understand there, because I believe that there is no cure that profits by medicine or any other cause approaching cauterization.
And the cause is contrary to that; and my understanding is that cauterization is the last resort of medicine only when one administers the methods of cure in some diseases, and those medicines do not concur, and just at the end of the cause one minimizes cauterization, and it profits thereby. And I see now that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to my understanding which understands the common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cauterization does not make a difference, as long as it is absolutely true, because I have already shown and proved that it does not do this except in certain bodies, and cauterization with gold is good and better than with iron, just as they say; but meanwhile, when you perform cauterization with fire on aurum, it is not to be declared, because it is unknown according to the quantity you wish for the roughness of the aurum, and since it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust over it ignition so that the aurum melts by the fire, and a case occurs in the fire where some plates are formed so that the artisan can see through the occupation of that.
And therefore, it is made to perform cauterization with iron in a way that we must be more lightly and more promptly guided towards the correctness of operation.
And I have already organized this chapter on cauterization according to chapters, and I have organized those from head to feet, so that it may be easier for the one asking about it.
The First Chapter.
This cauterization refers to the humidity and coldness that occurs on the surface of the accident, which has two causes: one is caused by soda and the other is caused by a torrential flow of rheumatic fluid, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and also due to excessive sleep, toothache, and yawning, and universally all diseases that come through coldness, such as paralysis, sogginess, apoplexy, and similar things in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is as follows: first, I command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine in the morning, for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the patient and their age and habit demands.
And then I command him to shave his head with a razor, and afterwards make it smooth between the hairs on top of a well-crafted bench, and have him rest his head on the stone floor.
And then pause the razor's edge on your palm above the nose between your eyebrows. But meanwhile, when your mouth says the middle part is reached, mark that place with a tent, and then ignite the olive cauterization of which this is the form:
And then pause that on the marked place with a tent, in a way that it descends, by which your thumb is gradually constricted little by little, and you revolve it.
And then lift your hand lightly and look at the place, and if you see that some quantity of bone has been uncovered on the skull, just as the amount of grain of errors, then raise your hand, and if it does not return to its original position with that iron, but is cooled down, until what I have said to you becomes visible.
And then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it over the place, and let it sit for three days.
And then pause on that spot surrounded by borders and let it stay there until the scar of fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with four-leaf gentian medicine until it is healed.
And they said that the more the wound remains open, the better it gets, so that it is more helpful and beneficial.
And they said that some of theirs should be cauterized with a red-hot iron into the bone, and hold the cauterization until some part of the specificity of the bone is tempered.
And then remove that which has been tempered with the bone, and then cure it.
And others said that with the cauterization, it reaches the end, and then presses on the bone with great force until the bone cracks, and this is the form of little alphetiation. And they think that from that place, the vapors of the head are released.
And the wound is kept open for a long time, and then it is cured until it is consolidated.
But to me it seems that these two species of cauterization are not visible from head to toe, but only in some men according to the way of fear; and leave it alone, I think, better is for health when it is so, because the head is revealed by solution of continuity like we have testified in other members, and even more so when the patient's head is of a fearful nature.
And the first species of cauterization is more saved and better, according to my opinion; and from that house and with that work there is health.
Second Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head in a patient, and they are prolonged in their condition, and use ointments, poultices, capes, emplasters, poultices, and similar things, and especially if it has already been cauterized with one cauterization which does not benefit or relieve the patient, then consider whether the head of the patient is prone to strong creation in its nature; and if not fearful and finds a great chill, then that cauterizes another cauterization, leaving a little bit. And then cauterize it on the crown of the patient's head with a cauterizing iron until the skull is divided. Cut the skull and expose the quantity of bone which we have counted, and then cauterize it with a cauterizing iron in the rear part of the head, in the place called "vas", where the wind pipe is located. And then lift your hand away from there, and do not expose the bone, for the patient will experience a great deal of pain that is different from all the other head cauterizations.
And you will say that this cauterization is in its place, for it is necessary to cauterize the crown of the head and the occiput with a more subtle cauterization than that which is used for the middle part of the head; and this is the form of it.
Third Chapter.
On Cauterizing Headaches Not Caused by Ancient Causes.
When headache pain is felt in the crown of the head or spreads to the eye, and evacuation with laxative medicines does not help, then another cure should be administered, which I have mentioned in the divisions of diseases; and if it does not benefit, there are two ways to cauterize: either by using acute medicine combined with a cauterization, or by using iron.
But cauterization with combined medicine is when you take a piece of aloes, scrape it off, and cut off the extremities at both ends. And then make an incision in the spot of the pain on the temple with a well-sharpened lancet until it is made into a small hole, so that it may be hidden.
And then strengthen it with a stopper made of descending constriction, and leave it for the space of three hours; and then remove the plaster and treat the aloes, and let the wound be open for two or three days, and then pause on that spot surrounded by borders until the place becomes firm.
And then cure it with gentian medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some combined medicines which I have written about in the two treatises on combined medicines.
But the iron cauterization according to this manner: ignite by cauterization of which this is the form:
and is called "claus clavilhs", because the head of it is shaped like a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small elevation.
And then pause on the spot of pain, and hold your hand steady - so that the iron is not scorched where it is left - and slowly revolve the small iron with speed.
And if the quantity of blood that is scorched by the specificity of the bone is like the majority of it, and lift your hand for this reason - so that the artery which is left is not scorched, lest a flow of blood comes.
And then immerse the cloth in saltwater and pause it on the spot, and leave it for three days; and then pause another cloth wrapped around the border, and cure with gentian medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize at the extremity of the scalpel according to the method, and be careful not to cut into an artery in this proper non-ancient headache.
Fourth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Ancient Headaches.
When you cure a headache with what we have said about the previous treatment and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not benefit and the disease is such that it does not reach the point where we have said about the first cauterization with medicine or with fire, then you must ignite the cutler's cauterization until it becomes white, because you signify on the spot of pain with a line of length equal to the majority of the same thing, or whatever; and pause your hand for one moment and strengthen that until you incise the artery and reach into the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which is damaged by mastication, and that the ligament not be scorched and the nerve which is affected by that, and that there be no spasmodic contraction.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut, because in the cutting of it there is fear, and especially to him who ignores what he is doing and is not studious or experienced; and leave the operation to begin.
And you will find in memory of the regimen of accidental blood flow according to your own manner, in your place in this book.
And if you see that this disease does not reach the point of this cauterization and you see that the patient's body is tolerable, then cauterize it in the middle part of the head just as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cauterization which we have said in the chapter on stretching the artery with two cloths, and it is a better cauterization and more conducive.
Fifth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Earaches.
When in the ear there is pain due to cold and it has been treated with laxative medicines and the other cure which I have mentioned in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cauterization, and this is the one called "puncta", of which this is the form:
And then place the puncta near the ignition, and be guided to the entire ear as if a wheel is turned around, or in the circuit of each example if the pain is in each. Hold the cauterization of the ear's root slowly and gradually as you have indicated the location with a tentative touch.
And if the cauterization of those points in the entire ear is done, and whichever one it may be, then cure the spots until they are healed.
Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Turtura.
Turtura which is cured and by cauterization it is nothing but the species that comes through phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that occurs due to dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of turtura with jerrals and capipurgies and guarguarisms, and your treatment does not bring relief, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: the first at the root of the ear, and the second a little below the temporal temple, and the third at the junction of two lips.
And pause your cauterization at the opposite part of the affected side, because softening only appears on the side that seems to be healing.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauterization in the right extremity of the ear, a little above the crown of the head, and on the temple another, the length of which is according to the length of the said thumb, and pause your hand with the cauterization until the quantity of the majority of the specificity of the bone is consumed.
And this is the form of the cauterization, and it is a species of the scalpel, the form of which is before us. But however subtle it may be, that which you see a little bit is what you must cut off in excess of unnecessary growth.
And then cure the spot with water as it proceeds until it is healed.
Seventh Chapter.
On Cauterizing Ancient Apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it with the water that we have said and your treatment does not bring relief, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize it with four cauterizations: on all the crowns of the head; and with the middle cauterization in the middle part of the head, just as we have said; and with the cauterization in the back of the neck. And the manner of the cauterization is made according to what has been said above.
And it has been cauterized at the mouth of the stomach; and it is more recent; and then it should be cured with water as it proceeds.
Eighth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Oblivion Caused by Phlegm.
It is necessary to give the patient in the beginning large jars and pills of serving medicines that clean the mind.
And then remove the cloth from the entire patient and place on the back of the neck an emplastrum described in the treatise on emplasters.
And pause that for a few moments, because it is the manner of cauterization. And do so according to that order which I have already said.
And therefore if by those means he is healed; and otherwise, then do to him three cauterizations in the back part of his head, which are descendents of the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the neck. And pause between each cauterization the thickness of a finger, and then cure the cauterization with water as it proceeds.
But if you add more and the patient is thus tolerant, then do to him the cauterization in the middle part; and if you desire greater addition, then immediately cauterize that on both crowns.
And then cure it until it is healed; and be the olive cauterization according to the form previously given.
Ninth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Parasites and Softening the Entire Body.
It is necessary for you to proceed with the softening of the head with jars and water as we have said; and then remove the cloth from the patient's head, and then cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle part of the head, and one on all the crowns of the head, and one on the back part of the neck, and three cauterizations on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the disease of softening the body of many and the patients are tolerant and the disease is strong, then immediately cauterize it with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and subsequently with one cauterization until it is consumed by the bone's motion, and lift your hand. And then cure it until it is healed, and this be olive cauterization.
Tenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Epilepsy.
It is not cauterized the epileptic, but that epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore it is necessary to soften the brain at the beginning with jars and other cure which we have said in the division when the disease is great and the patient is tolerant, except for medicines.
And if it is an infant who cannot tolerate medicines, then immediately administer guarguarisms and mastiguarists serving softening medicines, before this for many days, with the blessing of good food.
And then remove the cloth from the patient's head, and then cauterize it with one cauterization in the middle part of the head according to the previous manner, and another cauterization on the back of the neck, and on each crown of the head be cauterized. And if the patient is strong and tolerant, then immediately cauterize it with the cauterizations which I say, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And be olive cauterization according to what has been said previously.
But if the patient is an infant, then immediately pause subtle cauterization according to this manner.
Eleventh Chapter.
On Cauterizing Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted and gross phlegm, then immediately cauterize it with the cauterizations which we have said in the previous chapter, having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excess and decline into melancholy, and the patient's body is humid, then immediately give him to drink water that softens the brain of him according to what has preceded in the division.
And then remove the cloth from the patient's head, and then make a gentle circular motion on him around the circle, and then place it in the middle part of the head.
And the patient shall be seated comfortably, and held from all sides.
And then pause the liniment; and it is more worthy of ancient border of sheep's wool. And warm that over the fire with gentle heat by measure, which the patient has suffered when it is most in him. And then place that in the middle part of the head of him in the circle, and let it enter until he is cooled down.
And do so with the patient for one week at a time, with another regimen of good things until he is healed; or if you wish, cauterize it making small points according to what is best for him, without holding your hand with a cauterization thus ordered: this is a species of cauterization which moistens the brain with equality.
And then pause that wrapped in cloth or in gray flannel.
Twelfth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Water Descending into the Eye.
When you declare the beginning of water in the eye by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to drink to the patient water that softens the head of him, and guard it from all humidity.
And then place that in a bath of hot water for several days.
And then command him to wash his head, and cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle part of the head; and then cauterize it with two cauterizations on both temples if there is the beginning of water flowing from both eyes, or on one side if there is the beginning of water flowing from one eye.
And incise all the veins and arteries that are left by the bone; and be the cauterizations in that length on the latitude of the temples.
And be careful of bleeding when it is cauterized; and if you see any bleeding from it, stop it with some medicine that is at your disposal.
And you will find wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries and in the excision of those and caution in bleeding.
And some times it is cauterized in the vertebrae left between two bones with two cauterizations subsequently produced.
Thirteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Old Tears.
When the tears from the eyes are old and accumulated through the veins and arteries that are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that this is excessive and watery phlegm, then immediately cauterize it with a cauterization which we have recounted in the chapter on the beginning of water flowing into the eyes, and also with a cauterization in the middle part of the head and two cauterizations in the vertebrae left between two temples, and two cauterizations in the vertebrae left between two bones. And if you need to add something, then immediately cauterize it on the entire back of the eyebrow above the upper eyelid with a small cauterization.
Fourteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Stench from the Nose.
When you treat him with water as we have said in the division and your treatment does not produce relief, then prepare yourself and give to drink to the patient cochineal for three nights; and then remove the cloth from the head of him, and cauterize it with a middle cauterization and olive cauterization. And then cauterize it with a clove cauterization and two cauterizations on both upper eyelids left between the hair a little.
And be careful not to cut into that artery.
And of the clove cauterization, this is the form.
Fifteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Softening of Eyelids of the Eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by disease or humidity, then immediately cauterize that eyelid with a cauterization with this lunar cauterization; and this is the form of it:
And if you wish, then cauterize that over both upper eyelids a little with two cauterizations in every part, and be prolonged from the temples. And be the length of each cauterization according to the quantity of the upper eyelid.
And do not press too hard with your hand on the cauterization, but rather according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid is softened.
Sixteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Eyelid of the Eye When the Hairs are Converted to the Inner Partitions and Punch the Eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the inner partitions so that they punch the eye, cauterize it in those places according to two manners, whether it is by fire or by a medicine that combines.
If by cauterization of fire, command the patient to hold his eyes thus as those which are cleaned, until they are prolonged and equalized; and if it pains him, then immediately you should strengthen the eyes of him with a bandage so that no harm comes to them while the hairs are growing.
Then when they are grown and equalized, immediately pause the patient's head in your seat, and then sign above the eyelid of his eyes with a tentative sign, with a signal which is according to the figure of a mercurial leaf, and be the beginning of the signal near the hairs.
And then place it wrapped in alum water or in pectinate mucus over the eye.
And then ignite the cauterization of which this is the form of it.
And then cauterize over the figure which you have signaled, little by little, in many times, until the surface of the bone which is thus like a leaf of myrtle, appears properly.
And the sign of health for this operation is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and the hairs of it being elevated above the puncture of the eye.
And therefore elevate your hand and leave it so for three days, and then pause on top of it with cloth until the scar is educated. And then cure that with ointment until it is healed.
But if some cause returns for the hairs and they become painful again, and the eyelid is softened, then immediately do another time the cauterization over it just as you did previously.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid itself, then immediately cauterize it until it is elevated to its natural place and equalized, so that the hairs do not hurt the eye.
But the cauterization with a medicine that combines is this: you command the patient to hold his hairs until they are prolonged and equalized, and then make a form of a leaf of myrtle from cloth.
And then take one ounce of known saponin and one ounce of living cause. It seems like the text has ended! And then take what is here, and immediately mix those causes well, and make this with a fumigation so that it will not be cooled; and then expand the water on the paper which is made thus in the form of a leaf of myrtle, and pause over one eye or both; and pause below the eye wrapped in alum water, and the patient's head should be in your seat.
And then pause the said on the medicine and press it a little and not harm it until the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for biting is in it as from fire.
And therefore when you perceive that he endures the biting, immediately let go of the medicine and make it clean with your said; then when the biting ceases, immediately remove the medicine and wash his eye with water; and then consider if at times the eyelid is raised as if it were washed away by fire or incision, for then you are well; and if not, return to that place of medicine where no medicine has been applied and do not disdain until your operation is equalized and the eye is constricted.
And then pause on top of it with cloth until the bone of adjustment is eradicated, and then cure that with ointment or another substance until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to carefully watch over your operation with diligent vigilance so that no residue of medicine falls into the eye; and if the eyelid becomes softened and some cause from the hairs hurts the eye after a few days, then immediately repeat your medicine on that place where the eyelid has become softened, and just as you did at the beginning, and then send it back until it is healed.
And this is the form of leaf of myrtle.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to magnitude and smallness, and therefore according to this is made your contraction.
And may not be hidden the way of rectitude to him who studies in this art.
Seventeenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Fistula that is in the Lacrimal of the Eye.
When you cure fistula with water as we have said in the divisions of diseases and it does not conform to your treatment, then immediately know that you must cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head on your seat, and hold his head steady between your knees in such a way that it is neither harmed nor agitated with his own head.
And then place it wrapped in alum water or in pectinate mucus over the eye of him.
And then ignite the cauterization of which this is the form:
which should be curved, like a shape of cane or the horn of a bull, from one end to which is made the cauterization.
And if you wish, it should penetrate into the other end. And if you wish, it should come out thus as if it were a test.
But in any case, the one that is curved is better for your work.
And then press on the fistula if it is open, and draw out from him the pus and dry that up. And if it is not open, then immediately work on it and extract the purulence from him.
And then pause on top of it with the cauterization which is well ignited, and take with your hand a little bit of the cauterized area from the edge of the nose, so that you do not err or trouble the patient, and then pause the cauterization in the gray matter of the eye and corrupt that.
And therefore if at the beginning of your cauterization it goes into the bone, that is good; and if not, then immediately repeat the cauterization one or two times, as needed; and leave it thus for three days, and then pause on top of it with cloth and surround it with drying ointment until it is healed.
But if it has been passed eleven days and it is not healed, then immediately pause on top of it with acute corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered and is rough as is fitting in your own chapter.
And there is another manner of cauterizing fistula which some people call "first" day: go to the location of the fistula and fill it with it; and then pause in that fissure as subtle as its form: And put into it the quantity of one ounce of melted lead; and take your hand with a gentle touch, and do not harm the patient so that the melted lead does not penetrate into his eye; and know that you pause on top of the patient's eye wrapped in alum water or water, for lead adheres to the location of the fistula and cures it through marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with the water that we have said about cauterization and healing, that is good; and if not, then immediately it is necessary to make a cut of the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to what will come in its proper place.
Eighteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Crack of the Pot.
Many times accidental cracks occur on the lips, and most often on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you cure those cracks with the water that we have said in the divisions and your treatment does not take effect, then immediately ignite the cauterization small cutlass according to this form that is learned:
And be the curvature of it according to the subtlety of a cutlery.
And then pause that initial application with care in those cracks until the cauterization reaches the bottom of the cracks.
And then cure that with ointment until it is healed.
Nineteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Fistula in the Mouth.
When in the throat of uvula or on the palate or on the roots of teeth an apostema forms and becomes swollen, and then breaks and is antiquated, and the swelling bursts and a fistula is formed, and you cure that but your treatment does not take effect, then immediately know that you must ignite cauterization according to the quantity received in the fistula; and then put that ignited thing into the track of the fistula, and take your hand until it reaches the bottom of it, and at the end of it do so one or two times; and then cure that with water as we have said about healing until it is healed.
And therefore if the pus is absorbed and is healed, that is good; and if not, then immediately it is necessary to uncover the location and expose the corrupted bone according to what will come in its own chapter.
Twentieth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Teeth and Softening Gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are damaged, and you cure them with medicines but it does not conform, then immediately place the patient's head on your seat, and ignite the cauterization in the form which will come to this, namely that you pause the quill over the tooth and insert into it the ignited cauterization rapidly, and take your hand a little so that the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth being reached.
And then lift your hand, and immediately repeat the cauterization several times according to your will.
And then the patient should blow his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, and then stop, because the damaged tooth is closed and the softened gum is strengthened and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Twenty-first Chapter.
On Cauterizing Toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness, or if there is a black spot or worm in it, or if the patient does not conform to the treatment with medicine, then immediately know that the cauterization in that case should be done according to two manners: either cauterizing with the border of cows, or cauterizing with fire.
Cauterizing with the border is that you take the border of cows and boil it in iron water, and then take a piece and wrap it around the extremity of the tent, and immediately immerse it in boiling border, and pause it over the painful tooth rapidly until it is cooled.
And then immediately repeat that several times until the virtue of fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, submerge the wool or cloth in the boiling border mentioned above, and pause it over the painful tooth, and then pause on top of that with hot iron until the iron reaches the bottom of the crack of the tooth.
But in any case, the cauterization with fire is that you attend to the quill of iron or steel, and it should be in the core of it some roughness and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterization in the form which will come, and pause it on the tooth and take your hand until the cauterization is cooled; and do so several times until the pain is relieved or within a day or two.
And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good border and hold it for an hour, and then spit it out; and this is the form of the cauterization.
And cauterize as you wish to the extreme limit according to what is possible for you.
And this is the form of the quill:
Twenty-second Chapter.
On Cauterizing Ulcers.
When ulcers are of phlegm and cold humors and do not obey digestion by medicines and you wish to ease the digestion of those slightly, then immediately ignite the cauterization curved in the shape which is this follows, having two extremities bulging so that the smoke of the cauterization rises on one side, and pause that ignited thing over that apostema once, and another if needed, until it reaches the bottom of the ulcer.
And if the ulcer is small, then immediately pause the cauterization according to the quantity of the ulcer, and then let it be for three days and pause on top of it with cloth wrapped in border until what the fire has burned off is relieved.
And then cure that with ointment, and tents, and cloths, until it is healed.
Twenty-third Chapter.
On Cauterizing Hoarseness of Voice and Constriction of Ale.
When the humidities come upon the canal of the lung, and especially when that is due to coldness of congestion, then it is necessary for the patient to be evacuated at first with laxative medicines, and then immediately cauterize that with fire on the root of the cough in the affected location.
And beware that you do not reach the lung with the cauterization nor burn too deeply into its fabric, but only a little.
And then cauterize that with another cauterization on the junction of the neck at the last vertebra of the spine. And let the cauterization be done in a similar manner as before.
And then cure that with water as is preceded, until it is healed.
Twenty-fourth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Disease of the Lungs and Cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are due to cold humidities and the patient has no fever nor phlegm, but is an old disease, then immediately cauterize that with two cauterizations on the furcula in the affected locations, one on each side; and another cauterization in the middle location of the breast between two nipples; and let the cauterization be done in a similar manner as before.
And if you wish, make your cauterization punctate with the point that is called puncture, in the form which precedes in the puncturing of earache.
And make points until they reach those places; and then cure that with water as is preceded, until it is healed.
And so the cauterizations have three steps which are for that: in one stroke you can do three cauterizations according to this form:

When the head of the assistant is dislocated due to lubricating humidities and does not stay in its place during its return movement, then it is necessary to reduce the dislocation and immediately reverse the patient's position onto his back or onto his side; and then elevate the cord which is in the anterior part of the citillic to the upper parts with your left hand, if the joint is dislocated backwards.
And then ignite the cauterization having two heads; and this is its form:
And then cauterize the cord until it penetrates into the other side; and the figure of cauterization will be like this: immediately ignite four cauterizations.
And several times it is adjusted according to this count, and because there are eight cauterizations.
And then pause on top of the cauterization with pores full of salt, and immediately make the patient adhere to tranquility, and let the member not be damaged for any time until it is comforted.
And if the dislocation is in the upper parts and it is thus done, then immediately cauterize on the muscle with a sharp-pointed cauterization or with multiple punctate cauterizations, because the joint is confirmed and the humidity is dried up and the patient is healed.
Twenty-sixth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Stomach.
When cold and many humidities come into the stomach, causing that external part of its congestion to be multiplied in it, and if you continue with the methods of treatment and do not conform, then it is necessary for the patient to be placed on his back, with his arms and legs stretched out, and immediately cauterize that with three cauterizations: one leaving a space of the size of a finger's breadth between the breast and the cauterization, sharp-pointed; and two cauterizations leaving the two sides of the cauterization, so that it forms a triangular figure; and elongate between them so that they do not interfere with each other to cause inflammation.
And if the depth of the cauterization is equal to the size of two-thirds of the thickness of the cord.
And let the figure of the cauterization be according to this form, with addition; and if you wish, cauterize with a large cauterization in the middle location of the stomach, according to this form; and this is one cauterization according to the form of a circle, according to this form:
And let the stomach be cauterized punctate to that which is frightened by this cauterization: and it is that you sense on the stomach point by point according to the quantity you wish with cloth, and then cauterize that with a cauterization at those points; and then cure that with the treatment which precedes until it is healed.
Twenty-seventh Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Fretted Vein.
When the patient has pain in the vein due to coldness or humidity or great swelling, and it is caused by excess flow from its normal condition, and the disease is cured with water as we have said and does not conform, then immediately place the patient on his back onto his cervical vertebrae, and sense three cauterizations according to this form and this quantity of cloth placed over the vein left of the hip bones, in which way it is customary for a man to lie down.
And let the space between each cauterization be according to the thickness of the finger, and let the cauterizations be in line with the length of a straight arm.
And do not compress the cloth on the cauterized part.
And if the quantity of water applied is equal to the quantity of the middle part of the thickness of the cord, and it is not adjusted further; and if the patient is standing on his feet; and if he is not standing, then let him be lying down, which has already stretched out his legs, and lifted his arms.
And if it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizations with a sharp-pointed cauterization, when it is according to your subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not process too much in the cauterization, and let the subtlety of all the cord be applied so that it is applied to all the body and reaches into the vessels, for this cord here is subtle; and know this.
Twenty-eighth Chapter.
On Perforating Ulcer of the Vein with a Cauterization.
When you endeavor to excise or ulcerate in the vein and you wish to know if that ulcer is in the flesh of the vein or in its tunica, then immediately if it is in the flesh of the vein, the patient's gravity and pain will increase without abatement.
And if it is in the tunica of the vein, then with great pain and many times that you have exhausted the physicians' cure for him.
Therefore it is necessary for the patient to be turned onto his back onto his cervical vertebrae; and then sense the location of the ulcer with cloth; and then ignite the cauterization which is similar to a rag, in the form which has preceded on the other page. And then cauterize with that and that cauterization until all the cord is burned away, until it reaches the groin, until healthy flesh appears.
And then cure that with the treatment of other ulcers until it is healed.
And do not use this form of cauterization unless you have studied medicine and it has been prolonged through experience, and many diseases have known its efficacy; but in this case, it may be bold to operate on this ulceration, yet nevertheless follow my counsel, and it will be better.
Twenty-ninth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Pleurisy.
The ancient cauterizations of the roots of aristology, which are applied to pleurisy coldly, according to this manner make it, and take one long, dry root that is found, and let it be of the thickness of a finger.
And then immediately submerge that in oil and ignite it at the fire, and then cauterize with a cauterization on that location which is between the continuation of the furcula and the neck; and two small cauterizations left guiding, one slightly inclining towards the side below the beard, and two cauterizations in what is declining between the fifth rib and the spine, declining slightly towards the back parts; and another cauterization in the middle location of the breast; and another on the stomach, and three cauterizations on the back parts; and one cauterization on that location which is between the two shoulders, and two cauterizations from the two sides of the breast, left guiding the cauterization which is between the two shoulders.
And do not compress your cloth with the cauterized part, but let it be in the manifest of the cord in operation.
And already some ancient ones have said that certain men among those who used iron cauterizations similar to rays and ignited them, and placed them on that location which is between the ribs, until they reached the ulcerated part and healthy flesh appeared, just as we have said in the apostema of the vein.
But in this perforation with a cauterization there is no fear, for if it happens that way soon, the fistula will occur at the location where there will be no healing.
Thirtieth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Melancholy.
When you cure the disease of melancholy with water as we have said in the division and do not conform to your treatment, then immediately cauterize there according to three methods, all of which are driutaries, one of which is that you make three or four linhan (lines) according to the length of the melancholy, following the figure of the cauterizations of the vein, the figure of which has preceded.
And let the thickness between each cauterization be that of a finger or slightly more, and the manner of the cauterization be the manner which we have said in the cauterizations of the vein equally.
And do not compress your cloth on the cauterized part; and let the patient be placed on his back.
And there is another manner of cauterizing, so that you ignite the cauterization having two points, which cause we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and elevate the cord which is in the endreyt (end) of the melancholy, where the patient's left side will be affected.
And let your elevation be such that you elevate the cord according to the length of the body, so that the cauterizations are made according to the latitude of the body.
And then insert the two points, ignite one, in that location where the cord will penetrate from the other side.
And then extract the cauterization; and thus make four cauterizations.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cauterization having three points.
And then cure the cauterization more thoroughly than you would have laid down to take it for too many days, because it is more certain that other causes precede in the treatment.
Thirty-first Chapter.
On Cauterizing Hydrocephalus.
Cauterizations are not applied in hydrocephalus, but only in acute cases properly.
When you cure the hydrocephalus with the methods of treatment which we have said in the division and do not conform to your treatment, then immediately it is necessary to cauterize with four cauterizations around the belly button, one on the stomach, one on the vein, one on the melancholy, two between the vertebrae of the back, one on the right side of the breast, and another on the stomach. And let the quantity of the depth of the cauterization be proportionate to the subtlety of the cord.
And then leave the cauterized part untouched for so long that it will take several days.
And do not evacuate the patient from treatment immediately after the cauterization with water as is necessary for two intentions to be added, and let it be hastened with the help of salvation.
The form of the cauterization with which the belly is cauterized is sharp-pointed according to its previous shape, and it is that one with which the back is cauterized is olive-shaped according to its previous shape.
Thirty-second Chapter.
On Cauterizing Feet and Legs.
When the feet are ulcerated in hydrocephalus and filled with serous water, it is necessary to cauterize the feet on the top of the foot between the auricular and anular bones, using no caustic water that is between the ear and wrist, and elevate your cloth with the cauterization and do not twist it; and then elevate your cloth and do not return all the way, because serous water resists.
And this is the form of the cauterization: And then make two cauterizations on both legs, and in each leg make a cauterization with the sharp-pointed end of the cauterization. And let the cauterizations be according to the length of the leg: one below the knee and the other above the middle part of the leg; and on each leg, two cauterizations.
And leave the wound open without treatment for a long time in order that some water may drain from it.
And then cure with those causes which we have said.
Thirty-third Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Abdomen.
When the abdomen is full and humid to the point where it debilitates the virtues, such as the digestive and retentive virtues in the stomach and intestines, and if the patient suffers from a cauterization of virtue exhibiting, then immediately cauterize that with a great cauterization on his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach, with the cauterization of the circle and four cauterizations in the subtle circle of the navel, with sharp-pointed cauterization; and with cauterization on the flank or two cauterizations.
And if sometimes the humidities abound and the patient can tolerate it, then immediately cauterize that on the navel and on the intestines, and firmly place two cauterizations on the stomach and near the groin, because it is perfect cure of the juice from which you will not err.
Thirty-fourth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Old Haemorrhoids.
When in nature there are old haemorrhoids or one of the gross humours that are fleshy or corrupted humidities, and they are cured with what we have said in the division and do not conform to your treatment, then immediately cauterize with three cauterizations on the remaining vertebrae of the little back and triangular, and one above the navel that descends by two digits.
And if you find that the patient's stomach is enfeebled and his food is not digested, and his face is often ulcerated, then immediately cauterize that on the stomach with a great cauterization according to what has preceded; and one on the vein, and another on the melancholy of him with sharp-pointed cauterization, and leave the cauterized part untouched for some time, and then cure him until he is healed.
Thirty-fifth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Abscesses.
When you excise an abscess, then immediately ignite the cauterization that is similar to a ray. And then insert that ignited thing into the excised abscess, and finally apply your cloth so that the cauterization reaches the orifice of the vein from which the blood flows.
And make it once or twice, because if there are many, then immediately cauterize each of them according to what we have recounted, and then cure those with the water that corresponds to their conditions until they are healed.
And if you cauterize with a great cauterization on someone, it is more certain in judgment.
Thirty-sixth Chapter.
On Cauterizing Fistulas that are formed in the natural parts of the body.
When nature does not obey the work which we have recommended in its place, and the patient is frightened by this, then let him be healed with a cauterization.
Therefore, when you find a fistula in the natural parts that is old and corrupted by blood and humidities, and thus what is most suitable for curing it is to attempt subtlety with it, and then know the quantity of its depth according to the preceding subtlety.
And then ignite the cauterization that is similar to a ray. And then place that ignited cauterization in this fistula, and according to the quantity in which the subtlety enters.
And iterate that cauterization over those corrupted bodies until they are completely burned away in one, two, or three iterations, according to the quantity of your need.
And beware of combustion of nerves and veins; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or intestines, then beware of all those places; and do not make it so until the fistula is in a place where it is not penetrating.
And then cure that place until it is healed.
And if the place is sealed, and all the matter has been removed from it, and it remains thus for a long time, then know that it is completely cured.
And if the matter is not removed from it, then know that it is penetrating or entering into the bone of the patient's body, or corrupting it, or falling under those causes from which a memory will be recalled in its place.
Thirty-seventh Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Tonsils.
When in the tonsils there is pain due to inflammation or gross ventosity, and because of this the patient's throat is dry, then it is necessary that you cauterize that on the tonsils with a cauterization on each tonsil with a sharp-pointed cauterization from which recall will precede.
And then cauterize with a small cauterization in the second one, so that three linear cauterizations will come to be, and thus they will be more certain in judgment.
Thirty-eighth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Bladder.
When debilitation and softening occur in the bladder due to inflammation and humidities, such that the patient no longer retains urine, then immediately cauterize that in the lower part of the bladder where the hairs of the navel begin, and cauterize with one cauterization on the right side and another on the left side.
And let the length of each cauterization be according to the quantity of the knots in the bone; and cauterize that with a cauterization in the lower part of the back, or with two cauterizations if necessary.
And let it be a sharp-pointed cauterization according to what is processed.
Thirty-ninth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Mare (i.e., the womb).
When inflammation and humidities occur in the womb, and because of this conception is prohibited, and the menses are corrupted and delayed, and pain occurs due to the shedding of them, then it is necessary that the place be cauterized with three cauterizations in the circle of the navel, just as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder; and one cauterization on the lower part of the back, or two cauterizations, and let the cauterization be sharp-pointed.
Fortieth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Dislocation of the Hip (Anca).
When humidities are poured out at the part of the hip, and causes of swelling occur in that location, and the sign is that the leg is prolonged above the other when compared between them. And the place of the dislocation is found in the lower part of the buttock.
Then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the part of the hip with a cauterization resembling a circle, as you have marked with subtlety in the circle of the part, and because the part falls in the middle of the circle.
And let it be the cauterization of which the form preceded in the cauterization of the stomach.
And if this cauterization is not present to you, then immediately cauterize that with three cauterizations and one great olive-shaped cauterization.
And let the cauterization be made according to the quantity of the subtlety of all the cord; and then cure that until it is healed.
Forty-first Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Sciatic Vein.

And if the patient says that the pain is below the hollow of the knee and near the cleft, then immediately cauterize that place with a single cutaneous cauterization.
And beware in all cauterization that you do not leave the cauterized area burning with nerve or great archery, and because of this it will be bad for your patient, causing harm or contractions.
And I have seen one and another of those whom I will cauterize on the crease, and ultimately in the cauterization, the fire becomes inflated until the tumor reaches its peak, and the focus is perforated and corrupted all over the foot. And then comes a strong solution of the belly, and then death follows.
And if the pain is in two parts together, cauterize each one according to this method.
And the wise men say that in the cauterization of the hip, this is the method: make it similar to a circle of iron, with the circumference being half the width of a palm; and let the orifice be according to the thickness of an almond or slightly less.
And within that circle is another third; and let the space between them be the quantity of the knots of the bone; and let those circles be above two parts; and let their length be one knot or two knots, and make in those margins a iron covering decently adorned with circles; and this is its form:
And then let it be ignited in the fire until it reddens and sends sparks, and then let it be placed on the part of the hip, the patient lying on their back. And therefore, cauterize that with three cauterizations that are rounded into one.
And then let that be left for three days, and then apply an ointment to it with borders, and leave the wound open for many days; and then cure that with remedies until it is healed.
Thus speaks Albucasis: "Oh, sons, we have used this type of cauterization sparingly due to the fear of its regard by those who look upon it."
But from good cauterizations on him who suffered them, and finds with that the place of his.
But cauterization with medicines that are adherent is when you make two circles having a perforated armlet in which the guaffo of the iron door should be inserted; and let the length of the walls in their naughtiness be two knots or as many as.
And if the space between each one is equal to the quantity of the thickness of the finger; and let them be above and below, and let them contain themselves within each other according to this form:
And then pause over the part of the hip where the patient is lying on their back, and compress your hand on the part of the hip; and then take cold water and pour it between the two circles, and let its quality be like a small fire, gradually increasing, and keep it for the quantity of an hour, and suffer the patient to endure the mordication and adjustment of him - since that mordication will be as if from fire - until the mordication ceases.
And then lift your hand with the instrument and wipe away the cold water from all of the hip with soft water.
And then leave that alone for three days and pause over it with borders until the blackness of the adjustment is renewed, and leave it so for some days, and then run away from him in shamefulness; this is the final result in judgment.
And then cure that with remedies until it is healed.
And if the pain is extended into the cleft or the knee, make him stand in water according to how it is made in the hip similarly.
And this is the method of cold water, and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Recipe of alkali and of non-extinguished cause in both halves of one, and mix them together and pause in a new wave of which the left part is perforated by a small hole, according to the quantity that enters into him.
And pause in the fons of one wave another wave enveloped, and pour over that alkali and living cause with soft water which absorbs them by one finger, and then compress them with your tied hand for good compression, and leave the hole that lets out the sharp water into the left part of the enveloped wave.
And then adjust all that water, and pour it over another living cause and another alkali renewed, for that labor is of strong sharpness, which is administered in many operations of medicine and in cauterization of other members, for the operation is like fire.
And some of the medicines, with which the hip is cauterized, are like this: tezizic and mel anacrat mixed with a substance that is dissolved in water.
And Gualia recounts the story of a man from ancient times who underwent an operation and was cured of hip and sciatic vein pain, and magnificently says that it is as if it were a marvel, and he declares that no other cure is needed, and because it has been healed in one moment just as recommended, for it has taken him to the bath and to the bed already satisfied with that.
And it is that he is pressed with certain vertigo, and if not found green, then take a fig leaf recently gathered; and mix it with a little gray powder and apply it to the hip where the pain is, or in the cleft, or in the knee, and tie it.
And let it be left for the quantity of three hours or until the patient has yielded to the adjustment.
And then put him in a bath and therefore when his body is reddened, introduce him into the sun, for the pain ceases and he is healed.
And know that it is not necessary to use cauterization with these medicines except when the evacuation of the body is proper.
But already Escorides has said that when in a wound of the goat the sciatic vein is cauterized, it brings relief to him; and let the cauterization be done according to this method: take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it between the toes of the foot and the shin.
And then take dried goat's flesh and fill it with fire until it is made into carbon; and then place it on the wool and leave it there until it is stretched. And then repeat this process, and do not cease to apply it until the sensation of the biting reaches into the hip and rests the pain.
And this method of cauterization is called "cauteri de vaquas".
Chapter 42.
On the Cauterization of Pain in Two Places.
Sometimes pain is in two places due to numerous causes, such as by bruising or piercing or excessive evacuation, and similar causes, by the infusion of wet and humid matter.
And the cauterization is done not on all these species, but only in this one which is made by effusion of wet matter.

But if meanwhile the ligament is softened, then it is necessary that it be very tight.
And then stop the ligament at day and night just as we have said.
And if the eye has already been reduced, that is good; and otherwise, then iterate the poultice with powders, stricture, and suction until it is healed.
Chapter 21.
On the Incision of the Eminence of the Uveal Tunic.
When there is an eruption in the uveal tunic and it bulges out and proceeds beyond the eyelids like a grain of raisin, and its shape is that of a man through this, and you wish to incise it, then the operation in this case is done as we have recounted, that you insert the needle into the root of the uvea on the side left and above, and then place another needle in which is double-thread from the part of the lacrimal, and make that penetrate and let the first needle follow according to its disposition; and then incise the location of the double thread and lift up with that the part of the uvea in the circuit of the needle, and strengthen that firmly.

Chapter 22.
On the Cure of Alconatis.
This disease which is called alconati is nothing more than pus that is lodged in the eye, resembling descending water and not being that.
But the manner of working on it is that you make the malady settle on the prepared and straight bed, and then take your own head in both parts and lift it up until you see the pus coming to the left side, and then be dried and not descend, and be stopped from flowing, and let the malady behold the causes just as it beholds.
And if it does not flow down, you know that it is water.
But if the descent of the pus is not prepared with water as we have said, then make the malady settle between your fingers and take a subtle spatula and pierce it over the pannicle, leaving a small portion to continue the conjunctiva with the tunic cornea in the crown (in the place where it should be), until the pus is forgotten.
Therefore, when it is forgotten, then you distill into the eye water that flows in which you have mixed honey with water in which you have already built fenugreek and honey.
And then be cured by other causes until it is healed.

Chapter 24.

Chapter 25.
On the Natural Warts on the Extremities of the Nose.
Many times is natural warts on the extremities of the nose, and it is magnified and swollen in several days until the wound is large enough to be seen.

And if the abscess is of lion's tooth and not of dark color, and when incision is possible in all that, then evacuate the malady and incise that without fear, and cure the place with what exists and constrain into being healed.

Chapter 30.
On the Extraction of Teeth.
Take care that you extract the tooth from its pain with all gentleness and quietness in the whole extraction of it, for there is no cause that should precede the removal of it when it is extracted, for it is a subtle substance into which it is excused in the extraction of it.
But when the malady is firmly seated in that tooth to be extracted, then you must be certain which tooth is the one that hurts, for many times pain deceives the malady and takes it to be in a healthy tooth, and you extract that one and then the pain does not cease until the sick tooth is extracted, for we have already seen this through the operation of barbers.
Therefore, when you are certain which tooth hurts, and what you know well, then it is necessary that you scrape in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth to the gum on all sides, and then extract it with those same said instruments or with fine forceps little by little until it comes out.
And then take hold of it with strong forceps that are good for speaking or extraction, and pause the head of the malady between your fingers which will keep it from hurting, and then extract the tooth according to straightness in manner so as not to break it, nor give the major malady greater pain.
And therefore if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments and place it alongside the tooth on all sides with facility and effort the removal of it just as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is cracked or corroded, then it is necessary that you complete with cloth that crack and strengthen it with the extremity of a subtle thread so that it will not be torn in the hour of your constriction upon it as you hold it.
And it is necessary that you work with great care and gentleness in the circuit of all parts of the gum, and guard your strength so as not to break it and leave a part of it behind, and return upon the malady through the malice which is greater than the first pain of it.
And be careful that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their haste and audacity over the extraction of theirs, without administering what we have recommended; for many times they bring upon men great maladies which are more difficult to extract than they should be, and the roots of their mouths become all inflamed or some of those or that you extract with some bones of the jawbone just as many times we have testified.
And then the extraction of it should be washed with mouth with vinegar or juice and salt.
And if it happens that fluxes of blood appear in this way, just as many times happen, then take some quantity of egg white and sprinkle it over the wound, and if you do not find that egg white to be effective, then cauterize.
The shape of the forceps and fine tongs with which the tooth is extracted at the beginning should be of long extremity, short handle and thick, in order that they may not bend when you must work with them.
And be just like times of thick handle in order that when you strain with those they may not bend, and be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron with descending shape and triple extremities, and in the extremities of those some teeth are placed one within another and strain through construction descent force, and sometimes the extremities of those take the form of a bird's beak called ciconia, so it is guarded, and they are of strong constriction.
