And if the membranes are not returned and the fetus is dead, then it is necessary that you insert those and extract the remains of the fetus or tie the body to her hand with a cloth and extract it with equality, because it will soon be forgotten.
When the fetus emits on its feet, then it is necessary that you push those into them, and accordingly, convert the small foot, and accordingly, make equal with it, and accordingly, take one foot of yours and stretch it little by little.
But when they are emitted into the thighs, then you command it to her that she may express herself, and make her sneeze with condiments, because it will soon be forgotten if God wills it.
And if it is not forgotten with that which we have recounted, then you return the small foot little by little until it pauses according to natural figure, because it will soon be forgotten with a lighter emission.
And if it is prohibited with all that which we have recounted, then take a poultice of althea and dissolved gum, and beat it well in the mortar for good beating, and accordingly, line it with water on the womb of the woman, at the lowest part of her belly. And accordingly, make that poultice cease in warm water, until it reaches the hypochondria.
And when the parts below of it are relaxed, then make it submit to the sub-fumigation of myrrh and sub-pause it for her. And when the sub-fumigation lasts for an hour, then make it cease on a bed, and accordingly, make her sneeze and stretch out her mouth, and take away from that, and press the lower part of her belly with gentle compression, because the fetus will soon be forgotten.
Emission of the Fetus laterally hanging from one of its arms. Be gentle in reducing her arm, but if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the lyre, and conceive the thighs of her with violent concussion, and accordingly, administer those which I and you have recounted to be poultices.
And if the childbearing is done, then make her cease on a bed, and accordingly, study on the reduction of the arm, and equalize the fetus according to natural figure, and make her sneeze and command her to compress herself until it is forgotten.
Emission of the Fetus on its neck, with its arms expanded and the flesh of her stretched out to both sides of her mother's. It is necessary that the midwife hold the hand of the fetus and accordingly turn it little by little, and make it equal with ease.
And when it is and what is equalized, then pause over the womb of her with that which we have recounted, namely oil and poultices.
And accordingly, command her to compress little by little, and when you have done this, then make her cease on a bed and command her to be inclined over the right side, and accordingly, command her to compress herself; and make her sneeze with condiments. The exit of the prepared fetus is above the shoulder.
When it is about to emerge from the mother's womb according to this manner, consider, and accordingly, you insert the second finger of your hand into her own fingernail until the humidity is evacuated.
And if the fetus is suspended over her face and neck, then you insert your finger into the umbilical cord, so that it may not be retained and die.
And accordingly, push the fetus into the lower parts until it is paused according to what is necessary, and command the woman to compress herself some times, and if God wills, it will be forgotten with a lighter emission.
The exit of twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are sometimes born, and some times not, nor three or four, but this is strange and does not happen often; however, there are causes natural and not living.
And among those, whether they be multiple or not, a second one is born, and are separated by ciphac, distinguish them into each bond in the umbilicus of each of them And some times they are forgotten thus as if it were only one fetus for lighter natural emission, and sometimes they are separated thus as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult to give birth and proceed according to what we have said about the unnatural figures, then you cure those thus as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what is done with ease and subtlety, and in delay, and is gentle according to all figure, according to how it is prepared for her by the engineer leading to health.
A reminder of what is formed in the womb from embryos and those that are aborted.
Some times are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and up to ten, and you must verify for me that a woman aborts at seven months, while another gives birth to all ten, which is caused by measurement of the glorious sages.
And thus it is necessary for the science of the midwife, since it is a small resemblance to this, and therefore pause at this with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the Extraction of the Fetus when it is Dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medication and it does not come out, and you are forced to use operation by hand, then it is necessary that you consider whether the woman is of good virtue and not affected by any of the accidents for which danger is feared over her.
Then it is necessary that the woman be elevated on a lyre over her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her thighs lifted.
And the minister should hold that of two parts or tie it on the lyre, so that her body does not stretch too much during the extraction of the fetus.
And accordingly, you moisten the mouth of the mother with oil and with the poultice of althea and fenugreek and with the seeds of lily.
And accordingly, the midwife takes her hand with those oils and poultices, and accordingly, inserts her hand with ease into the mother, and accordingly, seeks out the exact location where the fingers rest on the fetus.
And so located in that: then you consider if the fetus is prepared to descend on its own head, and accordingly, place your fingers on the temples of her, or on the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or below the beard, or at the furcula of her, or on the places suitable for the ribs, or below the hypochondria.
But if the descent is over her feet, then in the armpit, or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary to have the finger on the right hand, and pause the curvature of her at that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand with ease and place the finger in one of those places which we have said, until you achieve the desired result.
And accordingly, pause and place another finger or the third if necessary, in order to attract equality and not be stretched according to her rectitude only.
And thus it is good for all parts, in order that the emission of her may be alleviated as it is done in tooth for the eradication of her.
And it is necessary in her that which is between them to soften the extension; and if any part of her is retained, then the midwife should take some of her fingers with oil and insert them expertly and turn around with what is retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is forgotten, then the fingers should be pushed into the place where it is higher; and make it so that the whole fetus is forgotten.
But if the hand is emerged before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it through the constriction of her, then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped around it; and accordingly, extract it until all is forgotten, and insert it either at the junction of the hand or in the armpit.
And so it is necessary that you do the same on the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is constriction in the emission, or water is adjusted in the head of her, then it is necessary that you insert between the fingers, and break the head and extract the water, or use an instrument called "alundat", the form of which will be described with the forms of other instruments in the chapter which is appropriate to this.
And similarly do if the fetus has a large head by nature: and it is necessary that you insert it with a forceps, or take it with an alundat as we have said; and accordingly, extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is emerged and constricted at the furcula, then it should be cut open until the humidity which is in the parts is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obeys to emission, then you should insert the head as soon as possible according to what seems best to you.
And if the afterbirth of the womb is apostematic or in it there is hydroptic fluid, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the humidity which is in it flows out.
But if the fetus is on her feet, then the attraction of it is gentle and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is gentle.
But if it is constricted at the belly and parts, then it is necessary that you extract it with cloth which you will wrap around your hand, and cut open the belly and parts until the water which is in them flows out.
But if the other members are stuck and return to the head, then place it with your left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is swollen, then insert your hand into the pomegranate, and seek out that head, and attract it with those fingers, and accordingly, enter one or two fingers, and draw it out through her mouth.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an apostematic swelling which occurs to it, then it is necessary that you not trouble over it; but rather, administer effusion of humid and fatty causes. And administer poultices; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on her own ribs, then it is necessary that you insert it as much as possible; and administer water which we have said for a living fetus.
And if this is not possible, then insert it in the feet, and extract it.
And make sure that you do not leave any cause behind the second finger.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer the water which we have said for the cure of apostematic swellings that occur in the mother.
And if bloody flux occurs, then let it flow into stiptic waters and administer another cure.
And I myself have seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus, and accordingly, on top of that fire another pregnancy was undertaken, and accordingly, the dead fetus is another. It happened to me a long time ago that an apostema occurred in my own umbilicus; and it swelled up until it became hot as fire, and I began to sweat.
And I was called to the cure of it, and medicated it for a long time, but the wound did not consolidate.
And then I wrapped it with some plaster of strong attraction, and drew out one bone, and accordingly passed several days, and drew out another bone; and I was greatly amazed, as there was no bone in the womb.
And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
And then I examined the wound and drew out many bones from it, the woman existing in her own good disposition, and thus she lived in this way for a long time, recovering from a small part of the arm.
And I do not think it strange, but rather because in this is science and aid to that which the physician crafts with his hand for cure.
Of the forms of instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
The shape of the uterus which is open in the mother:
This is the shape of a strengthen in which are equalized the liberties, to which equalization are two vertebrae at two extremities of two feet. But however this vertebra must be more subtle than the strictor, and made of ebony or boxwood.
And the width of each staff should be two fingers and a half, and the margin of one side is equal to one finger, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle place between the two staffs there are two adjustments of those staffs which are already fixed, from which the length is most of one palm and a little more, and the width of each is two fingers or a little more.
And these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that they can be opened up with them when you rotate the two prescribed vertebrae.
Another similar form to that one, more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the likeness of forceps. But however, at the end of it there are two additions like times, and the length of those additions is equal to one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open her up with those, then you should cause the woman to lift herself on a lyre, and let her feet hang down, opening up what is between her ribs. And accordingly, work the instrument with your hand like you do with forceps, equalizing according to the quantity that you want of the appreciation of the mouth of the mother until she does what you want.
The shape of the uterus which they called "vertitge" in ancient times:
The shape of impulsion, with which the fetus is impelled:
The shape of amiability, with which the great head is contained:
And it is assembled like forceps with teeth at the end, just as times, and some times it is made long like forceps according to this form, just as times, with teeth like the teeth of a rasp which is inserted and contained. The shape of amiability few:
The shape of a finger having a spine:
The shape of a finger having two spines:
The shape of a spatula having two extremities at which the head is severed:
The shape of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when the more species of them are multiplied and prepared by the artists, as it is lighter to their operation and higher in quantity.
And you should not neglect those instruments regardless of what, because the necessity of them is irrepressible.
On the extraction of the second finger:
When the second finger is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary that you command the patient to retain her breath, and accordingly, make her snort with condensation, and strengthen your hand on the mouth of her and on her nose, and if by this means it has been extracted outside, so be it.
And if not, then you should take a cloth and pierce a hole in the cover of it, and pause on that spot where the mouth of the mother is open, as with calamus and rue and anise and camomile and Arabian senna and cinnamon and St. John's Wort. All these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the cloth, and pause that on the fire.
And accordingly, place a reed cane in the mouth of the mother, and keep it there until the evaporation comes to the concavity of the mother.
And accordingly, make her snort as we have said, and the second finger is extracted quickly.
But if the cure remains and is not extracted, then you should command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a poultice of althea, and accordingly, insert it into the canal and search for the second finger, and when you have found it, then take it and extract it little by little. But if it is annexed to the womb of the mother, then enter your hand according to what we have recommended, and when you have found the second finger, extract it little by little with rectitude so that the mother does not faint from the vehement attraction. But before all, it is necessary to be flexible on both right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recommended the cure with snorting and with medication from the cloth with herbs.
But if it is not extracted with all the causes that we have recommended, then beware that you do not fatigue yourself on that in iteration of abstraction, but rather, it is necessary that what has come out from there to the mouth of the mother lies at the end of the woman, and accordingly, crystallize that with a poultice and tetra-pharmaceutical; for that will make it putrid after some days and be dissolved and extracted.
But when it putrefies, it is lifted to the bad air of the head and stomach, and that leads the patient astray; and accordingly, it is necessary that sub-fumigations and conveniences are administered thereto.
But some of the Ancients have already experimented with sub-fumigation from Nazareth and dry figs.
The shape of an instrument by which the woman is sub-fumigated for the retention of menses and the second finger:
It is made of beryl or iron.
And it is placed with the subtle extremity in the canal and the broad extremity on the fire, and the sub-fumigation is placed on the arms of the fire.
And keep that there until that sub-fumigation is consumed and another iteration occurs.
On the cure of the child's unperforated navel:
Some children are born without a navel and their navels are not perforated, which already have a subtle and opaque cicatrix. Then it is necessary that the midwife pierces with her finger that cicatrix; and if not, then pierce it with a sharp spatula, and beware that she does not touch the lactating area.
And accordingly, place on it some wool soaked in wine and oil; and accordingly, cure that with a poultice until it is clean.
But if you fear that it may be opaque, then place a reed cane in the hole for several days, and stop when the child wants to pass.
And already an opacity of the navel occurs due to consolidation of the wound or apostematic swelling; therefore, it is necessary that this consolidation be inserted, and accordingly, cure it with the water we have said for the cure and with lead.
On the cure of fistulas that are left behind:
The fistulas that remain in the aftermath of childbirth, lower down near the navel and larger than those which remain by the anus outside or in the space of one part.
And it is a fistula or multiple fistulas.
And since that node is aged and flows with white or subtle pus-like liquid, and sometimes some of these fistulas are penetrated.
And those that are penetrated are known by the matter that is discharged from them through exit and windiness; and sometimes the patient uses a cathartic of exit, and very little is discharged from those red ones.
And some of those fistulas penetrate into the space of the bladder, and into the urethra of the penis; and some of those penetrating ones go into the junction of the womb and into the notch of the cervix.
And the way to know if a penetrating fistula goes into the anus and not into it is that you put your finger in the anus and enter a subtle probe of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no turbulence.
But if there is turbulence in that, then you should insert into it a subtle probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all nor does any cause of exit or redness or windiness proceed from the hole, just as we have said, then you will know that it is not penetrating, and accordingly, go to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urethra of the penis, then the significance of it is that urine will be discharged from it and prohibition of it to this effect that the place where medicine is consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the womb or into the bone and causing pain in the circulation, then the signal of it is that the probe will pierce here if there is no turbulence in the bone, and causing pain in the circulation of the part; and that from this place there will be pus-like discharge always; and that it does not hold with that medicine, nor is consolidated with a poultice.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the cure of these is the labor and vehemence of the foolish doctors over which I am fixed.
But in that which is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is expected according to what you have recommended and what I have tried.
And it is that the patient lies between your knees on his back and lifts up his hips towards you, with his legs bent at the knees, so that his womb is inclined towards his belly, and accordingly, insert a probe of lead or iron into the fistula if there is turbulence in it, until you know the location where the probe penetrates.
And if that patient feels pain around the navel, then it is necessary that you insert your finger into the navel.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe has already entered and is penetrating, or if you feel between your finger and that siphac or flesh, then you will know certainly that it is penetrating; and accordingly, do not trouble yourself about it, as we have said.
But however, some may say that it is healed in certain men's hearts.
And the medicine by which healing is expected in it is that you apply a subtle cauterizing fire according to the size of the fistula, just as has been preceded, and insert that ignited substance into the fistula until it spreads around the navel; and accordingly, repeat that process two or three times until you know that all those fleshy tissues adjusted to the fistula are like the feathers of an owl.
And accordingly, cure that with calques wrapped in leather until all those fleshy tissues are healed; and accordingly, cure that with medicines generating and consolidating flesh, and if it is healed, so be it; and if not, then do not expect it to be healed at any time by another cure.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate into the navel which is in the anus, but between that and the probe which is a veil of flesh or cicatrix, and sometimes the fistula is opened on the surface of the codon, then dry the codon from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it dried with the probe, and it will be in the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the end of the probe comes out, and through the probe is liberated and cut.
And accordingly, purify those fleshy tissues fistulated which are gathered like the beak of an owl and do not remain any cause.
But if a flux of blood comes sometimes between you and your operation when you are purifying those fleshy tissues, then use the milch that is and the least painful instrument is cauterization with fire or with acute medicine, for cauterization with fire adjusts two good habits: so it is adjustment of those adjusted fleshy tissues, and abscission of blood from excessive moisture.
And accordingly, cure that with calques wrapped in leather or in three-fold cloth until the wound is fully closed, and accordingly, cure the wound with hard flesh generating and consolidating.
And such medicines in which there is dryness and excess; when accordingly it is restored, it is already healed and you do not fear relapse.
But if the fistula has already reached the perineum of the anus and is prolonged from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and inquire about it.
And therefore, if you find the probe and it enters between you and her, it is veiled by cicatrix or flesh, and it is prepared for penetration, then do not perform an operation there except according to the way of faith and hope.
The cause is to administer in that place one of three ways: either to cauterize it as we have said; or to dry it so that you can achieve the conquest of it and insert the probe into the cure prepared for it, and do not proceed with drying until you are sure that you will not cut into the lactating area containing the navel, and that nothing will happen to the patient except by his own consent; and accordingly, cure that with water as we have said, because very little is needed for healing; or to lengthen that veil and remove that pus which dries it up there in the anus, just as we have said, either with a probe or another instrument of sharp extremity, and accordingly, purify those fleshy tissues fistulated which are in the drying process until you can perform percrustation; and accordingly, strive to achieve the restoration of all the wound through drying, and if the orifice above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the anus, it will be easier for the patient. And in some cases the fistula is finished according to this method: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is on the edge of the anus around the surface of the body with the coden and at the margin of the anus, then take hold of a perforated extremity, which is like an awl preparing the vessels according to this form:
and insert into that faithful package wrapped in five fingers or around those, and accordingly, insert the probe with faith into the fistula until you achieve the conquest of it.
But if it is penetrating in the margin of the anus proper to the outside, then you extract the probe from that hole just as you insert your finger into the anus; and extract the extremity of the probe and adjust the two extremities together, and strengthen each one, and leave it so for a day or two, and when you more deeply insert the probe into the flesh, strengthen it well until those fleshy tissues are inserted between the two extremities of the probe which fall apart.
And accordingly, cure the wound so that it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate, in whatever way you are prepared, but not in the perineum, because it is not your place to do so, lest you cut into the lactating area; and accordingly, make it heal until it is healed.
The form of the spatula with which the fistula is opened: its curvature is very sharp and the other part is non-sharp, so that you do not cut into what is not necessary, just as sometimes.
On the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows during the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are in two ways, because either they are between the anus like charcoal, or those that are like grass of rye. And some are small and large, and the blood flows from those at all times and is one, and many, and outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however, those that are outside the anus are according to the months of little humidity, from which citrine water or a small amount of blood flows with the body continuing, and according to the color of the skin.
And the cure for that which is outside the anus is that you command the patient to settle and to press it in so that the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take hold of it and suspend from the hooks or what you have with your nail, and accordingly, cut those at their roots.
But if the hooks are not held in those due to their humidity and softness, then take them with a rough cloth or with a piece of leather or with wool floss, and extract them with your fingers, and accordingly, cut those and powder some powders over them, suitable for the incision, so that they may be applied to those as cauterizing; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterization. And accordingly, cure those with another cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey evacuation, then anoint the patient with a cathartic in which there is a small biting, and wash it with that water which is in the anus, so that it may obey evacuation slightly when the patient has pressed.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of theirs is slight, and it is that you take those with your nail or that you take those with hooks, and cut them, and accordingly, cure those with water as we have said until they are healed.
And the one who will make an incision should administer suturing of them according to this method: take a needle-wrapped probe and insert it into the awl and accordingly, extract the hemorrhoids at the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the awl in the root of the other part, and wrap the two extremities of the probe in the more distant part of the awl, and so laterally; and strengthen the hemorrhoid with strong stitching, and accordingly, remove the needle and awl.
And do this to all of them, and leave one and not sew it up, for that reason the superfluity of blood may flow from that.
And accordingly, pause over the anus with cloth dipped in red oil or cerate; and pause that over the anus and command the patient to rest. And accordingly, leave it so that it can heal; and when it is healed, cure those with ointment or another cure until they are well.
And when they are old and not suitable for that medicine, then you must cut those with the point of a spatula or with your nail until they are made moist and the scab above is prevented from forming, which prevents consolidation; and accordingly, cure those until they are consolidated.
Then you must cut those with a reason more vehement than the first, until there is much bleeding and they are exfoliated; and accordingly, cure those until they are healed.
Know that Almesmir is the key, and it's not just a notch red on the skin according to its color like the head of a clavicle, and it's made all over the body and most especially in the parts below the shoulders and above the elbows, and accordingly, by these pains, you must learn how to manage them.
And then it is necessary to cut out what is in the circle of the key, and hold it with forceps or hooks, and eradicate its root; and accordingly, cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize it according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterization.
But truly, a verruga is a small, sharp, round fistula on the surface of the body, and many times they appear in children.
And the cure for it is that you stretch and cut it open, or that you strengthen it with a probe or a skin thread until it closes. And if you wish, cauterize it, as we have said, with fire or acute medicine.
But a formica is a small, fatty or fistula-like prominence on the surface of the body going forward, and when the pimple reaches it, it seems to be bitten by a formic insect, and it is made around the body.
And the cure for it is that you take a reed pen or a vulture's quill, and make it strong, and pause it over the formica until it contains the circle of the reed pen in the parts of it; and accordingly, revolve your hand with the reed pen around what is in the circuit of the formica, and pause it on the navel of the flesh, and that eradicates the formica from its root.
And if you wish, do this with an iron or steel reed, according to this form:
Be the upper part of the reed thin and subtle (not perforated), wrapped in such a way that when you apply it to the said area, it may be ablated and the revolution of it.
And if you wish, cauterize the formica according to what is said before in the chapter on cauterization of atheyl.
The form of the instruments that are administered to give catharsis.
Sometimes it is made cathartic of silver or lead or melted iron or malleted; and sometimes it is made from those small and large instruments according to those to which they are administered, for that which is administered in the cure of little children is small; and those whose buttocks are rough or sore should have their cathartics small.
The form of catharsis great and little.
The head of the reed pen above, to which the pouch is tied, should be broad according to this method; and there should be a distinction at the point where the pouch is tied in such a way as to resemble times.
And the extremity of it most distant, which is inserted into the anus, should be thick and dense like a lion's fur, going back to subtlety; and on one side of it there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the hole should be according to the size of the rays and slightly thicker than small.
And the pouch should be in which medicines of animal bladder or sheep's wool are placed, and the root of it should be a palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes, just as it is revolved; and if the space between the holes is the largeness of that.
And accordingly, insert the strong needle into those holes, which is of ten needles or nearby them; and adjust the pouch with it; and when the pouch is placed in it, be tight at the head of the cathartic between two distinguished parts with strong constriction, and accordingly, cathartize each hole: But the quality of cathartizing is that you fill the pouch with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and take care not to make it too hot or too cold.
And accordingly, have the patient lie on their back with their knees bent and their feet flat on the floor, and place one leg over the other as if they are sitting on a stool; and accordingly, apply some oil or album of honey or mucilage of fenugreek to the extremity of the cathartic; and accordingly, insert it into the anus with ease, and have the assistant take the pouch and express it with two hands and many strokes with vehemence until everything in the cathartic is evacuated into the bedpan; and accordingly, remove the cathartic and have the patient lift their legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces him to evacuate excessively, take as much as he can tolerate; and if he sleeps with it for the entire night, it is better in terms of purging.
But if you cathartize him in the diseases of intestinal flux and evacuation, then you must iterate the cathartic until he is cured.
And if there are hemorrhoids or apostemas (abnormal growths) in the anus, then you must make the cathartic very subtle and dense, like those used for children.
The cure for plagues.
And I have said in the division of the cure for plagues earlier that it is suitable for a free person, and I say so too, the cure for these with me and with medicines according to complement.
So I say that plagues are diversified according to how they are made and according to the place on which they are placed.
And the causes by which many times plagues are made are just like getting a blow from a peyra (a type of hammer), or an incision with a knife, or a piercing with a lance, or with a fist, or with an arrow, or similar to those many causes.
But the plagues that are on the parts of the body are just like those which appear on the head, or neck, or legs, or belly, or thigh, and similar to those of the members.
And I recommend the cure for some plagues, by which one paces this reasoning and rule on other plagues.
And I will start with the simple plagues of the head, for the memory of the complex ones will come at the beginning of the fourth chapter.
So I say that when a simple plague occurs on the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to a blow from a peyra (a type of hammer) or similar, and the wound has already become large and there are concerns about impending apostema (abscess), then you must apply fleubotomia (cupping) to the cephalic area at once, without delay; and extract blood according to the quantity of virtue present in it, unless there is some other cause that prohibits cupping, especially if the blood that has flowed from the plague is little.
And the cupping should be done on the opposite side of the affected area; and take care to keep the patient from taking in excess food, drink, or heavy victuals.
But if any prohibited cause exists, then reduce the food and do not approach meat or wine.
And apply poultice to the wound, if an abscess is forming, using warm oil or wine that has been made stiptic.

The treatment of ulcer and fistula.
Know that every wound and abscess when it becomes old and is made into an ulcer, and does not consolidate and grows a branch all the time and is not cut off, then, wherever it may be in any member, universally it is called fistula and we call it zuchem.

Forma de razori en la qual ha concavitat:
Forma de razori autra subtil:
Forma de autra razori de curvada extremitat:
Forma de rasori petit semblant a tenta:
Forma de inscisori autra minor:
Forma de un autre inscissoir; aquest semblant a ray, e la extremitat de lu es cum serra, e es exhibit en motz locs en la razio dels osses:
Forma de ray lo qual conveneys a rasio de aquel que es perforat dels osses:
E la extremitat de lu es triangulada e de aguda extremitat.
E es fayt de ferr de India, e semblantment cove que totas las causas que havem ditas de rasoris e de inscissoris e de serras.
De inscizio extremitatz e de la serratura dels osses.
Las extremitatz se poyresso o per causa intrinseca o per causa extrinseca, o cum tu auras medicat aquela corrupcio per curacio de aquellas medicinas e la curacio no comfereys, o vezes la corrupcio anar deves le membre la qual no percuteys denguna causa, lahoras cove que tu inscidas aquel membre entro aquo la hon acossec la corrupcio, per que le malaute evasesca per aquo de mort o de malicia que es major defeliment del membre.
E le senhal de aquel al qual accideys, es quel membre es fayt negre entro que sia cujat que foc la ja comburit, o se poyreys aprop la negror entro que la poyredura aquela ane entro aquel membre que siec lu e que prengua tot le cors; e donc coyta te am inscizio de aquel.
E semblantment si es causa de la corrupcio percussio de alcunas causas venenosas ayssi cum de scorpio mari o de vupera o de rutela e de semblantz.
E si la corrupcio o la percussio es en la extremitat del dit, lahoras tu inscideys le dit e no dones spaci a la corrupcio per que ane entro a la ma.
E semblantment si accedeys a la ma, lahoras tu inscideys aquela de la razit del focil, e no dones spazi a la corrupcio entro que prengua en le focil del bras.
E si envezeys aquel, lahoras inscideys le bras entro al coyde en la junctura.
E si passa outra la corrupcio e la vezes enviro le coyde, lahoras en aquel es la mort del malaute; e aministrar autra causa otra aquo en curacio es quantitat de vertut.
E semblantment fay del pe quan corrupcio envezeys le dit del pe, lahoras tu inscideys aquel entro ad un dels nozes.
E si pren en la pente del pe, lahoras tu inscideys tot le pe. Mays si pueja entro al denol, lahoras tu inscideys la camba entro a la junctura del denol.
E si la corrupcio ja es pervenguda sobre le denol, lahoras en lu no es engen sino dimissio, e layssar le malaute a la mort.
E la manieyra de inscidir le membre o de serrar lu es que tu strenhas le liament en la partida pus dejos la qual voles inscidir, e strenh autre liament sobre le loc; e extenda le ministre un liament a las partidas dejos, e extenda le ministra autra liament en sus; e tu separa la carn la qual es entre dos liamentz ain spatum lat entro que sia descuberta tota la carn; e aprop sia inscidit o serrat.

Another method for applying an ointment to restore fractures and dislocations and torsion: recipe of asafoetida, ladanum, acacia, enula, and myrrh, which is the root of saved mulberry, one drachma x; of myrrh and aloes, one drachma five; of alochil, one drachma twenty; all are to be crushed and sifted and mixed with aqua aloe or album of hen if the patient's complexion is scorched; and then use this ointment, for it has good composition and restores broken bones slightly, and gives strength to men.
Another method for applying an ointment that gives strength to fractures and torsion: recipe of myrrh and white altica one drachma ten; of myrrh and aloes one drachma five; of acacia one drachma six; of Armenian balsam one drachma twenty.
